<div id="review_2556028476" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2556028476" />
    <a title="NZLisaM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/79324789-nzlisam"><img alt="NZLisaM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521069706p2/79324789.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2556028476?book_show_action=true">Aug 02, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="NZLisaM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="NZLisaM" href="/user/show/79324789-nzlisam">NZLisaM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9781473553996" href="/book/show/42778078-the-turn-of-the-key">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=suspense">suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/79324789-nzlisam?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2556028476" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18096677921085653454"><i>
  <b>‘WANTED: Large family seeks experienced live-in nanny.'</b>
</i><br/><br/>When childcare worker, Rowan Caine, stumbled across the advert she couldn't believe her luck. It's the opportunity she'd been waiting for.<br/><br/>But mere months later she’s sitting on remand in a Scottish prison, accused of killing one of the children in her charge. Furiously scribbling letters to a top advocate (barrister under British law), she pleads with him to take her case.<br/><br/>
  <i>‘”I didn't kill that child. Which means someone else did. And t</i></span>
  <span id="freeText18096677921085653454" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>‘WANTED: Large family seeks experienced live-in nanny.'</b>
</i><br /><br />When childcare worker, Rowan Caine, stumbled across the advert she couldn't believe her luck. It's the opportunity she'd been waiting for.<br /><br />But mere months later she’s sitting on remand in a Scottish prison, accused of killing one of the children in her charge. Furiously scribbling letters to a top advocate (barrister under British law), she pleads with him to take her case.<br /><br />
  <i>‘”I didn't kill that child. Which means someone else did. And they are out there. While I'm in here, rotting.”’</i>
<br /><br />This was definitely the right book for me. As a former sole-charge nanny (both live-in and live-out), and in more recent years, regular pet-sitter, house-sitter, I've spent a significant amount of time in other people's houses, largely with only children and/or pets for company, so I found the subject matter in this book hugely relatable. I could feel Rowan's frustration as she struggled to grasp the smart house's various control panels, apps, and features, and as someone who once stayed in a property where during a nighttime power cut all the doors unlocked, because the battery on the back-up generator died, I know the feeling of being in a strange house with malfunctioning technology, and not being entirely sure what to do. Rowan's first day, the two older children disappear on her, playing/hiding in the expansive grounds, and she's frantically searching for them while trying to juggle a fretful baby. Again, I've totally been there, more than once. There were many other instances I could mention, but I've bored you enough with details of my life.<br /><br />However, even though <i>I</i> enjoyed the day-to-day routine of Rowan settling into her nanny position, I'm not entirely certain other readers will feel the same way. And a large portion of the book was devoted to this. It's a slow burn, alright! <br /><br />But, the more I think on it, the more convinced I am that I would've enjoyed it regardless, as you get to experience exactly what Rowan went through from the moment she arrived until the tragic end. You get to know the lay of the land so to speak, and feel Rowan's mounting uncertainty and fear, her slow realisation that something’s not right with the place.<br /><br />Strange occurrences in the night – creaking, footsteps, cold spots, missing keys, etc – beginning the moment Rowan arrived, also assisted in moving the plot forward, and upping the creepy ante. Technology played a big part in the <i>‘hautings'</i> making this a bit different from usual. The house itself was part restored Victorian/modern architecture which I found as unsettling as Rowan did. The wild, overgrown, neglected gardens, so different from the interior, heightened this feeling. Being an old house it did of course have an ominous history, and was rumored to be haunted, which as some of you know are two of my favourite gothic elements. <br /><br />The four children (aged 14, 8, 5, and 1) had complex, age appropriate personalities and behaviours. <i>Ruth Ware</i> even included Scottish dialogue, which I thought was a nice touch. Even though the entire book was written as a series of letters, it quickly morphed into present tense, with the protagonist occasionally pausing to address the recipient. I for one was grateful for this, as I wasn't fond of the beginning letter format as it was all <i>‘tell'</i> and no <i>‘show’</i>. It was an original set-up though, and the way it all came together in the end cemented this novel's 5 star rating for me.<br /><br />My favourite <i>Ruth Ware</i> crime/mystery by far.<br /><br />I'd like to thank Netgalley, Random House UK – Vintage Publishing, and Ruth Ware for the e-ARC.<br /><br />US Release Date: 6th August, 2019.<br />UK Release Date: 8th August, 2019.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18096677921085653454" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2810489897" class="readable"
              >

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2935252878" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2935252878" />
    <a title="Effy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26874718-effy"><img alt="Effy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603795864p2/26874718.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2935252878?book_show_action=true">Aug 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Effy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Effy" href="/user/show/26874718-effy">Effy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26874718-effy?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26874718-effy?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26874718-effy?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2935252878" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11715666450041049372"><p><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40489648.The_Turn_of_the_Key' title='The Turn of the Key by Ruth Ware' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Turn of the Key</a> was the first book I read from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9013543.Ruth_Ware' title='Ruth Ware' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ruth Ware</a> and it will definitely not be the last!</p><br/><p>The book is a <i>psychological thriller</i> infused with <i>Gothic</i> and <i>Victorian</i> elements. The story is unfolded in the form of letters written by Rowan Caine while she is in prison and addressed to a potential solicitor, narrating the events that led to her incarceration. Rowan is accused of murdering a child she was looking after and is resolved on unraveling her unspeakable truth that will set her free.</p><br/><p>T</p></span>
  <span id="freeText11715666450041049372" style="display:none"><p><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40489648.The_Turn_of_the_Key" title="The Turn of the Key by Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">The Turn of the Key</a> was the first book I read from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9013543.Ruth_Ware" title="Ruth Ware" rel="nofollow noopener">Ruth Ware</a> and it will definitely not be the last!</p><br /><p>The book is a <i>psychological thriller</i> infused with <i>Gothic</i> and <i>Victorian</i> elements. The story is unfolded in the form of letters written by Rowan Caine while she is in prison and addressed to a potential solicitor, narrating the events that led to her incarceration. Rowan is accused of murdering a child she was looking after and is resolved on unraveling her unspeakable truth that will set her free.</p><br /><p>This book was so <i>enthralling</i> and <i>riveting</i> that it instilled an ineffable sense of <i>trepidation</i> in me and made my heart beat fast in my chest. Given that I read this at night, alone in the house, the ceaseless sounds of doors squeaking, windows creaking and footsteps silently pacing in the attic made my heart palpitate with <i>fear</i>. The state-of-the-art Heatherbrae House which was equipped with surveillance cameras and ran on an app took on a life of its own and became a 'character' haunting the protagonist. The <i>atmospheric ambiance</i> of the book set the scene for unfathomable, inscrutable things happening and wreaked havoc.</p><br /><p>Rowan was an <i>unreliable narrator</i> since she made a secret of her identity and was not completely to be relied on. There was a number of <i>plot twists</i> I could not have possibly seen coming. The only thing that vexed me about this book was the <i>anticlimactic ending</i>. So much effort was made to build up <i>mystery</i> and raise a baffling <i>conundrum</i> only to come to such an <i>underwhelming ending</i>. I would also like to know whether or not those letters saw the light of day and extenuated Rowan's case.</p><br /><p>If you are a fan of <i>suspenseful thrillers</i> and <i>enigmatic riddles</i> this book may be worth reading.</p></span>
  <a data-text-id="11715666450041049372" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3262135393" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3262135393" />
    <a title="Beata" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47571190-beata"><img alt="Beata" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1505761623p2/47571190.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3262135393?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beata" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beata" href="/user/show/47571190-beata">Beata</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer3262135393&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3262135393" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1776163701168098828">The title gave me some hints regarding where I would be taken while reading this book, and my expectations were rather high. Unfortunately, it did not turn out to be a page-turner for me. For one thing, too much time is spent on the descriptions of the smart house, in my opinion. I was not interested in finding out how the house worked as I have some idea of this type of a house. Moreover, Rowan Caine seems an unstable character, which is surprising if you take her profession into account and th</span>
  <span id="freeText1776163701168098828" style="display:none">The title gave me some hints regarding where I would be taken while reading this book, and my expectations were rather high. Unfortunately, it did not turn out to be a page-turner for me. For one thing, too much time is spent on the descriptions of the smart house, in my opinion. I was not interested in finding out how the house worked as I have some idea of this type of a house. Moreover, Rowan Caine seems an unstable character, which is surprising if you take her profession into account and the time she has had her job. This remark of mine may be a little unfair, however, has Rowan really been able to supress her negative attitude to children successfully for so many years and yet remain employed as a nunny? Also, I was unable to find the situation in which a nanny, just employed, is left with two small children and the third one about to arrive all alone. I enjoyed the story of the poison garden and the mystery behind it most. <br />It a good read but nothing gothic or spectacular about it for me.<br />*A big thank-you to Ruth Ware, Random House and NetGalley for arc in exchange for my honest review.*</span>
  <a data-text-id="1776163701168098828" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AFWXtPt+UetFHbc9h7w6qPxt1lh79/kjsUVbHjj01ykTa5VgRDSxyCO9QUYZXccqAOLhHSTHr0eQkV5uznmxCQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dZsPYkhO+ncCeBkhg1BzNI3rwZwo7kx+XZv0p1SCnoNmpQ229wQaVGTY71odsY62cWT22XfeGhp8T/HXog/4ow==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18445441103359905957">Ruth Ware grew up in Sussex, on the south coast of England. After graduating from Manchester University she moved to Paris, before settling in North London. She has worked as a waitress, a bookseller, a teacher of English as a foreign language and a press officer. She is married with two small children, and In a Dark, Dark Wood is her début thriller.<br/><br/>Find her on twitter at <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.twitter.com/ruthwarewriter'>www.twitter.com/ruthwarew</a></span>
